      "mechanic_instructions": "The diagnosis is a clogged exhaust elbow and/or riser. This restriction is causing the localized overheating and triggering the engine alarm due to increased back pressure and insufficient cooling. You need to replace the clogged exhaust elbow and riser assembly. Follow these steps from Section 7B, 'Manifolds, Elbows And Risers':\n\n1.  **Disassembly:** Refer to 'Disassembly' on Page 7B-2. Disconnect battery cables, drain water from the manifold, elbow, and riser, disconnect exhaust and cooling hoses, and remove any interfering components. Then, remove the elbow and riser, and finally the exhaust manifold fasteners, discarding old gaskets.\n2.  **Cleaning and Inspection:** Refer to 'Cleaning and Inspection' on Page 7B-3. Clean all gasket material from mating surfaces. Inspect the metal around the exhaust outlet for corrosion and check the flatness of all gasket surfaces. If the manifold gasket surface is damaged or not flat, it should also be replaced (Page 7B-4).\n3.  **Installation:** Refer to 'Installation' on Page 7B-5. Use new gaskets (fire ring gasket with 4 slots) and apply a 1/8 in. (3 mm) bead of Quicksilver Loctite 510 Sealant (P/N 92-804874) around all holes on both sides of the gasket. Assemble components immediately.\n    *   Install the exhaust manifold to the cylinder head, torquing fasteners to 25 lb-ft (34 Nm) (Page 7B-6).\n    *   Install the new exhaust elbow to the exhaust manifold, torquing fasteners to 33 lb-ft (45 Nm) (Page 7B-2, 7B-6).\n    *   Reconnect all cooling hoses and exhaust hoses, ensuring double clamps are used and tightened securely (Page 7B-7, 7C-15).\n    *   Allow sealant to cure for 2-3 hours before starting the engine (Page 7B-5).\n    *   Reconnect battery cables.\n4.  **Final Check:** Start the engine and thoroughly check for fuel, exhaust, and water leaks (Page 7B-7). The metallic banging confirms that this event caused components like connecting rods, pistons, or valves to collide or bend.       "mechanic_instructions": "The fact that the distributor rotor is not turning is a critical observation. This means the engine's ignition timing mechanism is not functioning, which is why you have no spark. The distributor is driven directly by the camshaft. If the rotor isn't turning, either the distributor's drive gear is stripped, the distributor shaft is broken, or there's a more severe internal engine issue like a broken camshaft or timing chain. Your next step is to remove the distributor and inspect its drive gear and shaft for damage. Refer to 'GM EST Distributor Removal' (Source 21, Page 4B-26) and 'Disassembly' (Source 29, Page 4B-27) for the procedure.",
